Detect: uneven load metrics — one partition/shard with far higher throughput, lag, or storage; skewed key distribution. Reshard safely: choose a better key (higher cardinality / more uniform — e.g. composite or hashed key, avoid monotonic/low-cardinality keys), then migrate without downtime: dual-write to old and new sharding, backfill historical data, switch reads over, then decommission the old. For Kafka, create a new topic with new partitioning and replay (don't just increase partitions — it scrambles key mapping). Plan key design up front; resharding is expensive, so over-provision and pick keys that distribute evenly while preserving needed locality/ordering.

On SIGTERM: (1) flip the readiness probe to down so the load balancer stops sending new HTTP traffic (drain). (2) Stop accepting new work — pause the queue consumer (stop polling) and reject new requests. (3) Finish in-flight requests/messages up to a grace timeout (Spring's server.shutdown=graceful), committing offsets only for completed messages. (4) Release resources (close pools, flush buffers) in @PreDestroy. Kubernetes: set terminationGracePeriodSeconds > your drain+processing time and use a preStop hook. Ensure idempotency so any redelivered in-flight messages (after the timeout kills them) are safe. Goal: no dropped requests, no lost/double-processed messages.

Use an Anti-Corruption Layer (ACL) at your service's boundary — a translation layer (Adapter + Facade) that converts the other team's model/terms/semantics into your domain language and back, so their model never leaks into and corrupts yours. Define an explicit contract (published API/events) between the bounded contexts and version it. Decide the context-mapping relationship (customer-supplier, conformist, partnership) and whether you integrate via sync API or async events. The ACL isolates you from their changes and lets each team evolve independently — essential when models genuinely differ.

True exactly-once across Kafka + an external card processor isn't achievable atomically, so engineer effectively-once: (1) consume with at-least-once. (2) Before charging, check an idempotency/dedup store keyed by orderId; if already charged, skip to emitting. (3) Charge using the processor's idempotency key (so the processor dedups even if you call twice). (4) Record the charge result and the consumed offset/orderId in one DB transaction; write the receipt event to the Outbox in that same transaction. (5) A relay publishes the receipt (at-least-once); downstream consumers dedup by receipt ID. Net: no double charge, no lost receipt — exactly-once effect, achieved via idempotency + outbox, not magic delivery.

Use shadow traffic / dark launching (a form of the Strangler pattern): mirror real production requests to the new service in parallel without using its responses (the old service still serves users). Compare outputs (a "diff"/parity checker, e.g. GitHub Scientist-style) to validate correctness and measure performance on real traffic with zero user risk. Once parity and performance are proven, gradually shift real traffic via canary (1% → 100%) behind a feature flag/router, with instant rollback. Ensure shadowing doesn't cause side effects (no duplicate charges — stub/sandbox external writes in shadow mode). Combine with contract tests.

  • Services (by capability): Catalog, Cart, Order, Inventory, Payment, Shipping, User/Auth, Notification, Search, Reviews — each owns its data (DB-per-service).
  • Edge: API Gateway (routing, auth, rate limiting) + BFFs for web/mobile; CDN for static + cacheable reads.
  • Communication: sync REST/gRPC for queries; events via Kafka for state changes; Outbox for reliable publishing.
  • Consistency: Saga (orchestrated) for checkout (reserve inventory → charge → create order → ship) with compensations; eventual consistency + idempotency; atomic conditional updates to prevent overselling.
  • Queries: CQRS read models / Elasticsearch for product search and order history.
  • Resilience: timeouts, circuit breakers, bulkheads, retries+DLT, graceful degradation, autoscaling.
  • Security: OAuth2/JWT, zero-trust per-service authz, secrets vault, TLS/mTLS.
  • Ops: observability (logs/metrics/traces + SLO alerting), CI/CD with contract tests, canary/blue-green deploys, expand-contract DB migrations, multi-AZ/region for HA.
